And in al-Khulasa: It is not proper for a menstruating woman to recite Quran or touch it except with a wrapper, and ritual impurity (hadath) prevents touching, and both janabah and nifas (postpartum bleeding) prevent, and intercourse without ghusl is [invalid]. He said: The junub may read the Torah and Gospel. Thus narrated from Muhammad and al-Tahawi; this narration is not accepted. May Allah be pleased with him, and upon it is fatwa. In al-Nihayah and others: When a female teacher menstruates, she should teach the children word by word and pause between the two words according to al-Karkhi; according to al-Tahawi, she teaches half a verse. In al-Tafri' there is consideration of al-Karkhi's statement, for he holds that a verse and less than a verse are equal in prohibition if done with the intention of reciting Quran, and less than a verse applies to the word; but if understood as teaching without intending Quran, then it is not restricted to the word. Then in many books, it is restricted to the menstruating teacher, justified by necessity due to the length of menses, and apparently it is not permissible for the junub. But in al-Khulasa: The later scholars differed on teaching by the menstruating woman and junub; the most correct is that there is no harm if she teaches word by word and her intention is not to recite a complete verse. It is better if her intention is not to recite Quran. His statement: ('and touching it except with a wrapper') i.e., the menstruating woman is prevented from touching the Quran because of what al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak, saying its chain is authentic, from Hakim ibn Hizam: 'When the Messenger of Allah sent me to Yemen, he said: Do not touch the Quran except when you are pure.' They also used as evidence His statement: 'None touch it except the purified' (56:79). The apparent meaning in al-Kashshaf is the validity of using this as evidence here if the sentence is made a description of the Quran and its wording in a hidden book protected from other than the near ones of angels; none else sees it. And they are the radiant lamp: It is not permissible for them to read the Torah, Gospel, and Psalms because all are the speech of Allah. His statement: ('He said, may Allah be pleased with him') i.e., the author of al-Khulasa. His statement: ('And in al-Tafri' there is consideration...') - he said in al-Nahr: I say: Rather it is correct, for al-Karkhi, though he prohibits less than a verse, but by that which makes one called a reciter, and that is why they said that spelling out the Quran is not disliked. It is not hidden that by teaching word by word, one is not considered a reciter, so pay attention to this useful restriction. Some scholars related from Mulla Ya'qub Pasha: His statement: 'less than a verse' means from compound phrases, not single words, because he permitted the menstruating teacher to teach word by word. This supports what al-Nahr said, and similarly supported by what is in Sharh al-Munyah, where it says that spelling out for the junub and teaching children letter by letter, i.e., word by word, with pauses between each two words according to al-Karkhi. According to al-Tahawi, it is not disliked if he teaches half a verse with pauses between them. And he said before: It is appropriate to restrict the verse to the short one whose less than it is not the length of three short verses, for if one recites the amount of Surat al-Kawthar, he is considered a reciter even if it is less than a verse, such that prayer is valid with it. In al-Siraj: Our later scholars said: If a menstruating or postpartum woman is a teacher, it is permissible for her to prompt the children word by word and pause between the two words according to al-Karkhi, and according to al-Tahawi, they teach half a verse, a whole verse, but do not prompt them a complete verse. His statement: ('and it is better if his intention is not to recite Quran') - some scholars said: There is consideration in the condition of the author of not intending recitation, because if he does not intend recitation, then it is not restricted to the word, as previously established that Quran exits from being Quran by intention. And this condition was not mentioned in al-Nihayah, al-Siraj, al-Zahiriyyah, al-Dhakhirah, nor in Fath al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of a menstruating woman (and junub) touching and reciting the Quran, and teaching it to children. The core ruling: a menstruating woman should not recite Quran or touch it without a wrapper (like a cloth cover). The proof is the hadith from Hakim ibn Hizam and the Quranic verse 'None touch it except the purified'. However, an exception is made for a teacher due to necessity. Two views: al-Karkhi allows teaching word by word with pauses; al-Tahawi allows teaching half a verse. The distinction is whether the teacher intends to recite Quran or just teach. If she teaches word by word and does not intend to recite a complete verse, it is permissible. Similarly, a junub is prohibited from reading Torah, Gospel, Psalms as they are divine speech. The passage also discusses that spelling out (tahajji) is not disliked for a junub because he is not reciting in the Quranic sense. The later scholars (mutakhkhirin) prefer the view of permissibility for the menstruating teacher out of necessity, provided she does not intend to recite a complete verse. The condition of intention is debated: some argue that if one does not intend Quran, then even a complete verse might be permissible, but the preferred view restricts it to less than a complete verse.

Key Terms
الحائض (al-ha'id): A woman in the state of menstruation.
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
التهجي (al-tahajji): Spelling out the Quran letter by letter or word by word without reciting continuously.

A menstruating woman must not touch the Quran except through a barrier, based on the hadith and Quranic verse, but necessity for teaching creates an exception.

Exception for Teaching: Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on teaching exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions under which a menstruating female teacher may teach Quran according to later Hanafi scholars, and differentiate between the views of al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi.

Core Idea
A menstruating teacher may teach word by word with pauses, as long as she does not intend to recite a complete verse.

While the general rule prohibits a menstruating woman from reciting Quran, necessity (darurah) leads to an exception for teachers. The Hanafi scholars disagree on the details: al-Karkhi permits teaching word by word, while al-Tahawi permits half a verse with pauses. The later authorities prefer the permissive view, provided the teacher does not intend to recite a complete ayah. This lesson unpacks that ikhtilaf and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Al-Karkhi: teaches word by word (kallimah kallimah) with pauses. Al-Tahawi: teaches half a verse (nisaf ayah) with pauses. Both avoid reciting a complete verse.
2
Understand the basis of the ikhtilaf
Al-Karkhi holds that even less than a verse is prohibited if it resembles recitation. Al-Tahawi considers half a verse as not constituting complete recitation.
3
Note the later scholars' preference
The later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) in al-Khulasa and other works choose the permissive view: no harm if she teaches word by word and does not intend a complete verse.
The condition of intention is debated; some say if she does not intend Quran at all, even a full verse may be allowed, but the precaution is to stick to less than a verse.
4
Apply the conditions in practice
A menstruating teacher must pause between words to avoid continuous recitation. She also must not intend the words as Quranic recitation but as teaching.
The same rule applies to postpartum woman (nifas) and, according to the stronger view, also to junub, though some restrict it to menstruating teachers.
5
Recognize the scope and limits
The exception is for teaching children who cannot learn from others. It is not a general license for the menstruating woman to read Quran for personal study.
Teaching adults would also be permissible under similar conditions if necessity exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخلاصة : ولا ينبغي للحائض أن تقرأ القرآن ولا تمسه إلا بغلافه ومنع الحدث المس ومنعهما الجنابة والنفاس وتوطأ بلا غسل بتصرم قال والجنب أن يقرأ التوراة والأنجيل. كذا روي عن محمد والطحاوي لا يسلم هذه الرواية . الله رضي عنه وبه يفتى .اهـ. وفي النهاية وغيرها وإذا حاضت المعلمة فينبغي لها أن تعلم الصبيان كلمة كلمة وتقطع بين الكلمتين على قول الكرخي، وعلى قول الطحاوي تعلم نصف آية اهـ. وفي التفريع نظر على قول الكرخي فإنه قائل باستواء الآية وما دونها في المنع إذا كان ذلك بقصد قراءة القرآن وما دون الآية صادق على الكلمة، وإن حمل على التعليم دون قصد القرآن فلا يتقيد بالكلمة ثم في كثير من الكتب التقييد بالحائض المعلمة معللاً بالضرورة مع امتداد الحيض وظاهره عدم الجواز للجنب لكن في الخلاصة: واختلف المتأخرون في تعليم الحائض والجنب والأصح أنه لا بأس به إن كان يلقن كلمة كلمة ولم يكن من أن قصده يقرأ آية تامة اهـ . والأولى ولم يكن من قصده قراءة القرآن كما لا يخفى . قوله : (ومسه إلا بغلافه) أي تمنع الحائض مس القرآن لما روى الحاكم في المستدرك وقال صحيح الإسناد عن حكيم بن حرام قال : لما بعثني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى اليمن قال : لا تمس القرآن إلا وأنت طاهر واستدلوا له أيضاً بقوله تعالى لا يمسه إلا المطهرون) [الواقعة: ٧٩] فظاهر ما في الكشاف صحة الاستدلال به هنا إن جعلت الجملة صفة للقرآن ولفظه في كتاب مكنون مصون عن غير المقربين من الملائكة لا يطلع عليه من سواهم وهم السراج الوهاج : لا يجوز لهما قراءة التوراة والإنجيل والزبور لأن الكل كلام الله تعالى. قوله : (قال رضي الله عنه الخ) أي صاحب الخلاصة قوله : ( وفي التفريغ نظر (الخ قال في النهر أقول : بل هو صحيح إذ الكرخي وإن منع ما دون الآية لكن بما به يسمى قارئاً ولذا قالوا لا يكره التهجي بالقراءة، ولا يخفى أنه بالتعليم كلمة لا يعد قارئاً فتنبه لهذا التقييد المفيد .اهـ. ونقل بعض الفضلاء عن المولى يعقوب باشا ما نصه : قوله ما دون الآية أي من المركبات لا المفردات لأنه جوّز للحائض المعلمة تعليمه كلمة كلمة .اهـ. وهذا مؤيد لما قاله صاحب النهر، وكذا يؤيده ما في شرح المنية حيث حمل قولها ولا يكره التهجي للجنب بالقرآن والتعلم للصبيان حرفاً حرفاً أي كلمة كلمة . القطع بين كل كلمتين على قول الكرخي، وعلى قول الطحاوي لا يكره إذا علم نصف آية مع القطع بينهما. وقال قبله : وينبغي أن تقيد الآية بالقصيرة التي ليس ما دونها مقدار ثلاث آيات قصار فإنه إذا قرأ مقدار سورة الكوثر يعد قارئاً وإن كان دون آية حتى جازت به الصلاة اهـ. وفي السراج قال أصحابنا المتأخرون : إذا كانت الحائض أو النفساء معلمة جاز لها أن تلقن الصبيان كلمة كلمة وتقطع بين الكلمتين على قول الكرخي، وعلى قول الطحاوي تعلمهم نصف آية نص آية ولا تلقنهم آية تامة قوله : ( والأولى ولم يكن من قصده قراءة القرآن قال بعض الفضلاء: في اشتراط صاحب عدم قصد القراءة نظر، لأنه إذا لم يقصد القراءة فلا يتقيد بالكلمة لما تقدم أن القرآن يخرج عن القرآنية بالقصد ولم يذكر هذا الشرط في النهاية والسراج والظهيرية والذخيرة، وكذا في فتح الخلاصة
And in al-Khulasa: It is not proper for a menstruating woman to recite Quran or touch it except with a wrapper, and ritual impurity (hadath) prevents touching, and both janabah and nifas (postpartum bleeding) prevent, and intercourse without ghusl is [invalid]. He said: The junub may read the Torah and Gospel. Thus narrated from Muhammad and al-Tahawi; this narration is not accepted. May Allah be pleased with him, and upon it is fatwa. In al-Nihayah and others: When a female teacher menstruates, she should teach the children word by word and pause between the two words according to al-Karkhi; according to al-Tahawi, she teaches half a verse. In al-Tafri' there is consideration of al-Karkhi's statement, for he holds that a verse and less than a verse are equal in prohibition if done with the intention of reciting Quran, and less than a verse applies to the word; but if understood as teaching without intending Quran, then it is not restricted to the word. Then in many books, it is restricted to the menstruating teacher, justified by necessity due to the length of menses, and apparently it is not permissible for the junub. But in al-Khulasa: The later scholars differed on teaching by the menstruating woman and junub; the most correct is that there is no harm if she teaches word by word and her intention is not to recite a complete verse. It is better if her intention is not to recite Quran. His statement: ('and touching it except with a wrapper') i.e., the menstruating woman is prevented from touching the Quran because of what al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak, saying its chain is authentic, from Hakim ibn Hizam: 'When the Messenger of Allah sent me to Yemen, he said: Do not touch the Quran except when you are pure.' They also used as evidence His statement: 'None touch it except the purified' (56:79). The apparent meaning in al-Kashshaf is the validity of using this as evidence here if the sentence is made a description of the Quran and its wording in a hidden book protected from other than the near ones of angels; none else sees it. And they are the radiant lamp: It is not permissible for them to read the Torah, Gospel, and Psalms because all are the speech of Allah. His statement: ('He said, may Allah be pleased with him') i.e., the author of al-Khulasa. His statement: ('And in al-Tafri' there is consideration...') - he said in al-Nahr: I say: Rather it is correct, for al-Karkhi, though he prohibits less than a verse, but by that which makes one called a reciter, and that is why they said that spelling out the Quran is not disliked. It is not hidden that by teaching word by word, one is not considered a reciter, so pay attention to this useful restriction. Some scholars related from Mulla Ya'qub Pasha: His statement: 'less than a verse' means from compound phrases, not single words, because he permitted the menstruating teacher to teach word by word. This supports what al-Nahr said, and similarly supported by what is in Sharh al-Munyah, where it says that spelling out for the junub and teaching children letter by letter, i.e., word by word, with pauses between each two words according to al-Karkhi. According to al-Tahawi, it is not disliked if he teaches half a verse with pauses between them. And he said before: It is appropriate to restrict the verse to the short one whose less than it is not the length of three short verses, for if one recites the amount of Surat al-Kawthar, he is considered a reciter even if it is less than a verse, such that prayer is valid with it. In al-Siraj: Our later scholars said: If a menstruating or postpartum woman is a teacher, it is permissible for her to prompt the children word by word and pause between the two words according to al-Karkhi, and according to al-Tahawi, they teach half a verse, a whole verse, but do not prompt them a complete verse. His statement: ('and it is better if his intention is not to recite Quran') - some scholars said: There is consideration in the condition of the author of not intending recitation, because if he does not intend recitation, then it is not restricted to the word, as previously established that Quran exits from being Quran by intention. And this condition was not mentioned in al-Nihayah, al-Siraj, al-Zahiriyyah, al-Dhakhirah, nor in Fath al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of a menstruating woman (and junub) touching and reciting the Quran, and teaching it to children. The core ruling: a menstruating woman should not recite Quran or touch it without a wrapper (like a cloth cover). The proof is the hadith from Hakim ibn Hizam and the Quranic verse 'None touch it except the purified'. However, an exception is made for a teacher due to necessity. Two views: al-Karkhi allows teaching word by word with pauses; al-Tahawi allows teaching half a verse. The distinction is whether the teacher intends to recite Quran or just teach. If she teaches word by word and does not intend to recite a complete verse, it is permissible. Similarly, a junub is prohibited from reading Torah, Gospel, Psalms as they are divine speech. The passage also discusses that spelling out (tahajji) is not disliked for a junub because he is not reciting in the Quranic sense. The later scholars (mutakhkhirin) prefer the view of permissibility for the menstruating teacher out of necessity, provided she does not intend to recite a complete verse. The condition of intention is debated: some argue that if one does not intend Quran, then even a complete verse might be permissible, but the preferred view restricts it to less than a complete verse.

Key Terms
الحائض (al-ha'id): A woman in the state of menstruation.
الجنب (al-junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl.
التهجي (al-tahajji): Spelling out the Quran letter by letter or word by word without reciting continuously.
الضرورة (al-darurah): Necessity that makes permissible what is otherwise prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) regarding a menstruating teacher's method of teaching Quran?
A) She may teach normally but avoid touching the mushaf.
B) She may teach word by word with pauses, not intending a complete verse.
C) She must only teach through writing, not speaking.
D) She may teach half a verse continuously without pauses.

Key Takeaway
Necessity permits a menstruating female teacher to instruct by word-by-word method with pauses, avoiding complete verse recitation, as per later Hanafi preference.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Touching the Quran Without a Wrapper: Prohibition for the Impure
Ruling with proof: prohibition of touching Quran for impure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching the Quran for a person in major impurity, identify the proof, and distinguish between attached and separate wrappers.

Core Idea
Touching the Quran without a wrapper is haram for the impure, but necessity permits teaching word by word.

This lesson explores the foundational rule that a menstruating woman or junub cannot touch the Quran directly. The ruling is based on a hadith and Quranic verse, but the definition of 'wrapper' (ghilaf) affects application. We will trace the proof and the scholarly interpretations of the wrapper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The source states that the menstruating woman (and by extension junub) is prohibited from touching the Quran (mas al-Quran). Determine the exact hukm level (haram) and note the exception for touching through a wrapper (ghilaf).
The matn says 'wa musahu illa bighilafihi' – touching it except with its wrapper.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites a hadith from Hakim ibn Hizam: 'La tamass al-Quran illa wa anta tahir.' Also, the verse 56:79 'None touch it except the purified.' Identify both proofs and their strength (zanni al-thubut for hadith, zanni al-dalala for verse).
The hadith is narrated in al-Mustadrak; the verse is interpreted as a description of the Preserved Tablet or the Quran.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
For the hadith, the imperative 'لا تمس' indicates prohibition; the condition 'إلا وأنت طاهر' implies that touching without purity is forbidden. For the verse, if taken as a description of the Quran, it conveys an order (amr) to be pure when touching.
The commentary discusses two interpretations of the verse; the stronger Hanafi view is that it supports prohibition.
4
Define the ghilaf
The passage presents two views: the ghilaf is the attached leather cover (al-jild al-musharraz) or a separate covering like a pouch. Determine which view is relied upon (al-mufta bihi) and why it matters for the ruling.
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah preferred the separate covering; this allows touching the mushaf when covered by a pouch.
5
Note the scope of prohibition
The prohibition applies to touching the written text of the Quran, not the blank margins of a page. Also, it applies to any object with Quranic writing (e.g., a dirham, a wall). Understand the exception for teaching (next lesson).
This is derived from the text's discussion of 'touching the Quran' versus 'touching the mushaf'.

كتاب الطهارة - باب الحيض
ومسه إلا بغلافه ومنع الحدث المس ومنعهما الجنابة والنفاس وتوطأ بلا غسل بتصرم
قال
والجنب أن يقرأ التوراة والأنجيل. كذا روي عن محمد والطحاوي لا يسلم هذه الرواية . الله رضي عنه وبه يفتى .اهـ. وفي النهاية وغيرها وإذا حاضت المعلمة فينبغي لها أن تعلم الصبيان كلمة كلمة وتقطع بين الكلمتين على قول الكرخي، وعلى قول الطحاوي تعلم نصف آية اهـ. وفي التفريع نظر على قول الكرخي فإنه قائل باستواء الآية وما دونها في المنع إذا كان ذلك بقصد قراءة القرآن وما دون الآية صادق على الكلمة، وإن حمل على التعليم دون قصد القرآن فلا يتقيد بالكلمة ثم في كثير من الكتب التقييد بالحائض المعلمة معللاً بالضرورة مع امتداد الحيض وظاهره عدم الجواز للجنب لكن في الخلاصة: واختلف المتأخرون في تعليم الحائض والجنب والأصح أنه لا بأس به إن كان يلقن كلمة كلمة ولم يكن من قصده يقرأ آية تامة اهـ . والأولى ولم يكن من قصده قراءة القرآن كما لا يخفى . قوله : (ومسه إلا بغلافه) أي تمنع الحائض مس القرآن لما روى الحاكم في المستدرك وقال صحيح الإسناد عن حكيم بن حرام قال : لما بعثني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى اليمن قال : لا تمس القرآن إلا وأنت طاهر واستدلوا له أيضاً بقوله تعالى لا يمسه إلا المطهرون) [الواقعة: ٧٩] فظاهر ما في الكشاف صحة الاستدلال به هنا إن جعلت الجملة صفة للقرآن ولفظه في كتاب مكنون مصون عن غير المقربين من الملائكة لا يطلع عليه من سواهم وهم السراج الوهاج : لا يجوز لهما قراءة التوراة والإنجيل والزبور لأن الكل كلام الله تعالى. قوله : (قال رضي الله عنه الخ) أي صاحب الخلاصة قوله : ( وفي التفريغ نظر (الخ قال في النهر أقول : بل هو صحيح إذ الكرخي وإن منع ما دون الآية لكن بما به يسمى قارئاً ولذا قالوا لا يكره التهجي بالقراءة، ولا يخفى أنه بالتعليم كلمة لا يعد قارئاً فتنبه لهذا التقييد المفيد .اهـ. ونقل بعض الفضلاء عن المولى يعقوب باشا ما نصه : قوله ما دون الآية أي من المركبات لا المفردات لأنه جوّز للحائض المعلمة تعليمه كلمة كلمة .اهـ. وهذا مؤيد لما قاله صاحب النهر، وكذا يؤيده ما في شرح المنية حيث حمل قولها ولا يكره التهجي للجنب بالقرآن والتعلم للصبيان حرفاً حرفاً أي كلمة كلمة . القطع بين كل كلمتين على قول الكرخي، وعلى قول الطحاوي لا يكره إذا علم نصف آية مع القطع بينهما. وقال قبله : وينبغي أن تقيد الآية بالقصيرة التي ليس ما دونها مقدار ثلاث آيات قصار فإنه إذا قرأ مقدار سورة الكوثر يعد قارئاً وإن كان دون آية حتى جازت به الصلاة اهـ. وفي السراج قال أصحابنا المتأخرون : إذا كانت الحائض أو النفساء معلمة جاز لها أن تلقن الصبيان كلمة كلمة وتقطع بين الكلمتين على قول الكرخي، وعلى قول الطحاوي تعلمهم نصف آية نص آية ولا تلقنهم آية تامة قوله : ( والأولى ولم يكن من قصده قراءة القرآن قال بعض الفضلاء: في اشتراط صاحب عدم قصد القراءة نظر، لأنه إذا لم يقصد القراءة فلا يتقيد بالكلمة لما تقدم أن القرآن يخرج عن القرآنية بالقصد ولم يذكر هذا الشرط في النهاية والسراج والظهيرية والذخيرة، وكذا في فتح
المطهرون من جميع الأدناس أدناس الذنوب، وما سواها إن جعلت الجملة صفة لكتاب مكنون وهو اللوح، وإن جعلتها صفة للقرآن فالمعنى لا ينبغي أن يمسه إلا من هو على الطهارة من الناس يعني مس المكتوب منه ا هـ . لكن الإمام الطيبي في حاشيته ذكر صحة الاستدلال به على الوجه الأوّل أيضاً فقال : فالمعنى على الوجه الأوّل أن هذا الكتاب كريم على الله تعالى ومن كرمه أنه أثبته عنده في اللوح المحفوظ وعظم شأنه بأن حكم بأنه لا يمسه إلا الملائكة المقربون وصانه عن غير المقربين فيجب أن يكون حكمه عند الناس كذلك بناء على أن ترتب الحكم على الوصف المناسب مشعر بالعلية لأن سياق الكلام لتعظيم شأن القرآن. وعن الدارمي عن عبد الله أن بن عمرو النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال القرآن أحب إلى الله تعالى من السموات والأرض ومن فيهن ا هـ . وذكر أنه على الوجه الثاني إخبار في معنى الأمر كقوله الزاني لا ينكح إلا زانية) [النور: ٣] ١ هـ. وتعبير المصنف بمس القرآن أولى من تعبير غيره بمس المصحف لشمول كلامه ما إذا مس لوحاً مكتوباً عليه آية وكذا الدرهم والحائط، وتقييده بالسورة في الهداية اتفاقي بل المراد الآية لكن لا يجوز مس المصحف كله المكتوب وغيره بخلاف غيره فإنه لا يمنع إلا مس المكتوب. كذا ذكره في السراج الوهاج مع أن في الأول اختلافاً فقال في غاية البيان وقال بعض مشايخنا المعتبر حقيقة المكتوب حتى إن مس ومس مواضع البياض لا يكره لأنه لم يمس القرآن وهذا أقرب إلى القياس والمنع أقرب إلى التعظيم ا هـ . وفي تفسير الغلاف اختلاف؛ فقيل الجلد المشرز، وفي غاية البيان مصحف مشرز أجزاؤه مشدود بعضها إلى بعض من الشيرازة وليست بعربية، وفي الكافي والغلاف الجلد الذي عليه في الأصح، وقيل هو المنفصل كالخريطة ونحوها المتصل بالمصحف منه حتى يدخل في بيعه بلا ذكر ا هـ . وصحح هذا القول في الهداية وكثير من الكتب وزاد في القدير ولم أر من نبه على ذلك فليتأمل قوله : (قول المصنف ومسه إلا بغلافه) قال في النهر : ولم أر في كلامهم حكم مس باقي الكتب كالتوراة ونحوها فظاهر استدلالهم بالآية اختصاص المنع بالقرآن اهـ. وفي حاشية الرملي: وهل يجوز في المنسوخ أن يمسه المحدث أو يتلوه الجنب فيه تردد والأشبه جوازه فيما نسخ تلاوته وأقر حكمه لأنه ليس بقرآن إجماعاً كما في شرح مختصر الأصول لابن الحاجب للعضد، وإذا كان هذا فيما أقر حكمه فمن باب أولى الجواز فيما نسخ تلاوته وحكمه اهـ أقول: ولا يخفى عليك بما قدمناه من العلامة الحلبي وغيره أن المنع من تلاوة المنسوخ من القرآن أولى، ثم رأيت بعض الفضلاء قال المشهور أن العلامة العضد شافعي فلا يصلح ما قاله دليلاً لمذهبنا، وقد تقدم أن ما نسخ تلاوته وحكمه كالتوارة ونحوها فتلاوته للجنب ومن بمعناه مكروهة على الصحيح كما اعتمده الحلبي لأن ما بدل منه بعض غير معين وكونه منسوخاً لا يخرجه عن كونه كلام الله تعالى كالآيات المنسوخة من القرآن، وأما مسه فقد علم حكمه مما نقله القهستاني عن الذخيرة
And touching it except with its wrapper, and the event prevents touching, and both (menstruation and post-partum) and janabah prevent touching, and she (menstruating woman) is entered without bath (but) with (time) passing. He said: And the junub should not read the Torah and the Gospel. Thus it is narrated from Muhammad and al-Tahawi, but this narration is not sound; (al-Allamah?) may Allah be pleased with him, and with it fatwa is given. End. In al-Nihayah and others: And when a female teacher menstruates, it is appropriate for her to teach the boys word by word and separate between two words according to al-Karkhi, and according to al-Tahawi she teaches half a verse. End. And in al-Tafri', there is consideration (that) according to al-Karkhi, for he holds that the verse and what is less than it are equal in prohibition if that is with the intention of reciting the Quran, and what is less than a verse applies to a word; and if it is carried on teaching without intention of Quran, it is not restricted to a word. Then in many books there is restriction to the menstruating female teacher, justified by necessity with prolongation of menses, and its apparent meaning is that it is not permissible for the junub. But in al-Khulasah: And the later scholars differed about teaching of the menstruating woman and the junub, and the most correct is that there is no harm if he teaches word by word and his intention was not to recite a complete verse. End. And the better (view) is that his intention was not to recite the Quran, as is not hidden. His statement: (And touching it except with its wrapper) meaning the menstruating woman is prevented from touching the Quran because of what al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak and said it is authentic chain from Hakim ibn Hizam who said: When the Messenger of Allah sent me to Yemen, he said: Do not touch the Quran unless you are pure. And they also used as proof His statement: 'None touch it except the purified' [al-Waqi'ah:79]. So the apparent meaning of what is in al-Kashshaf is the validity of using it as proof here if the sentence is made a description of the Quran and its wording in a hidden Book preserved from other than the near ones of the angels, none can see it except them. And al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: It is not permissible for them (menstruating woman and junub) to read the Torah, Gospel, and Psalms because all are the speech of Allah. His statement: (He said, may Allah be pleased with him, etc.) meaning the author of al-Khulasah. His statement: (And in al-Tafri', there is consideration) etc. He said in al-Nahr: I say: Rather it is correct, for al-Karkhi, even if he prohibits what is less than a verse, but it is by that which he is called a reciter, so they said it is not disliked to spell (letters) in recitation, and it is not hidden that by teaching word by word he is not considered a reciter, so be mindful of this beneficial restriction. End. And some virtuous people narrated from al-Mawla Ya'qub Pasha what follows: His statement: 'what is less than a verse' meaning from compounds, not singulars, because he permitted for the menstruating female teacher to teach it word by word. End. And this supports what the author of al-Nahr said, and likewise what is in Sharh al-Munyah supports it where it carries her saying: And it is not disliked to spell (letters) for the junub with the Quran and teaching boys letter by letter, i.e., word by word, with separation between every two words according to al-Karkhi, and according to al-Tahawi it is not disliked if he teaches half a verse with separation between them. And he said before it: It is appropriate to restrict the verse to the short one that does not have what is less than it equal to three short verses, for if he recites the amount of Surat al-Kawthar, he is considered a reciter even if it is less than a verse, until prayer is permissible with it. End. In al-Siraj: Our later scholars said: If the menstruating or post-partum woman is a teacher, it is permissible for her to dictate to the boys word by word and separate between two words according to al-Karkhi, and according to al-Tahawi they teach them half a verse, a complete verse, and do not teach them a complete verse. His statement: (And the better (view) is that his intention is not to recite the Quran). Some virtuous people said: There is consideration in the condition of the author of not intending recitation, because if he does not intend recitation, then it is not restricted to a word, as previously mentioned that the Quran exits from being Quran by intention, and this condition is not mentioned in al-Nihayah, al-Siraj, al-Zahiriyyah, al-Dhakhirah, nor in Fath. The purified from all impurities, the impurities of sins, and other than that if the sentence is made a description of a hidden Book, which is the Preserved Tablet, and if it is made a description of the Quran, then the meaning is: it is not befitting that it should be touched except by one who is in a state of purity from people, meaning touching the written part. End. But Imam al-Tayyibi in his gloss mentioned the validity of using it as proof on the first aspect as well, saying: The meaning on the first aspect is that this Book is noble in the sight of Allah, and from its nobility is that He established it with Him in the Preserved Tablet and magnified its rank by ruling that none touch it except the near angels, and He protected it from other than the near ones, so it is necessary that its ruling among people be likewise, based on that arranging the ruling upon the appropriate description indicates causation, because the context of the speech is to magnify the rank of the Quran. And from al-Darimi from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr (?) that the Prophet said: The Quran is more beloved to Allah than the heavens and the earth and those in them. End. And he mentioned that on the second aspect it is a report in the sense of a command, like His statement: 'The adulterer does not marry except an adulteress' [al-Nur:3]. End. And the expression of the author with 'touching the Quran' is better than others' expression with 'touching the mushaf' because his speech includes if one touches a tablet on which a verse is written, and likewise a dirham and a wall, and his restriction to the surah in al-Hidayah is incidental, rather the intended meaning is the verse. But it is not permissible to touch all the mashif written and others, unlike other things, for it does not prevent except touching the written. Thus it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, although there is a difference in the first: In Ghayat al-Bayan: And some of our shaykhs said: What is considered is the reality of the written, such that if one touches the white spaces, it is not disliked because he did not touch the Quran, and this is closer to analogy, and prohibition is closer to veneration. End. And in the interpretation of the wrapper there is difference: It is said it is the stitched leather, and in Ghayat al-Bayan: A mushaf with stitched parts, some parts bound to others from al-shirazah, and it is not Arabic. In al-Kafi: The wrapper in the most correct view is the leather that is on it, and it is said it is the separate one like a pouch and similar that is attached to the mushaf so that it is included in its sale without mention. End. And this view is certified in al-Hidayah and many books, and increased in al-Qadir: And I have not seen anyone who pointed that out, so let it be considered. His statement: (The author's statement: 'And touching it except with its wrapper') He said in al-Nahr: I have not seen in their speech the ruling on touching the remaining books like the Torah and the like. The apparent meaning of their using the verse as proof is the restriction of the prohibition to the Quran. End. In al-Ramli's gloss: And is it permissible for the one in hadath to touch the abrogated or for the junub to recite it? There is hesitation, and the more similar is its permissibility in what has been abrogated in recitation and its ruling remains, because it is not Quran by consensus, as in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Usul of Ibn al-Hajib by al-'Adud. And if this is in what its ruling remains, then a fortiori permissibility in what has been abrogated in recitation and ruling. End. I say: It is not hidden from you, from what we have presented from al-Allamah al-Halabi and others, that prohibition of reciting the abrogated part of the Quran is more appropriate. Then I saw some virtuous people said: The widespread view is that al-'Allamah al-'Adud is Shafi'i, so what he said cannot be a proof for our school. And it has preceded that what has been abrogated in recitation and ruling like the Torah and the like, its recitation by the junub and those like him is disliked on the correct view, as al-Halabi relied on, because some part of it has been replaced by something non-specific, and being abrogated does not remove it from being the speech of Allah, like the abrogated verses of the Quran. As for touching it, its ruling is known from what al-Qahistani narrated from al-Dhakhirah.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a Hanafi commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the restrictions on a menstruating woman (ha'id) and a person in a state of major impurity (junub) regarding sacred texts. The discussion is organized around several rulings from the matn. Firstly, touching the Quran is prohibited without a wrapper (ghilaf). The proof is a hadith from Hakim ibn Hizam and the Quranic verse (56:79) 'None touch it except the purified.' The commentary explores different interpretations of the verse, whether it refers to the Preserved Tablet or the mushaf, and concludes that it supports the prohibition for the impure. Secondly, the matn indicates that a junub should not read the Torah, Gospel, or Psalms, as they are all divine speech. However, there is a minority narration from Muhammad and al-Tahawi that is not relied upon; the fatwa is on the prohibition. Thirdly, a significant portion discusses the permissibility of a menstruating female teacher teaching Quran to children. The text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Karkhi allows teaching word by word with a break between words, while al-Tahawi allows teaching half a verse. The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) lean towards permissibility with conditions, especially if the teacher does not intend to recite Quran but merely teach. The commentary emphasizes that the dispensation is due to necessity (darurah) as her menses may be prolonged. For a junub, there is more restriction. Fourthly, the definition of 'wrapper' (ghilaf) is discussed: whether it is the leather cover attached to the mushaf or a separate pouch. The most correct view is the separate covering, and it affects the ruling on touching. Finally, the passage touches on touching and reciting abrogated (mansukh) scriptures: there is hesitation, but the relied-upon view is that it is permissible to touch what has been abrogated in recitation but whose ruling remains, because it is no longer Quran. However, for the junub, reciting even abrogated parts is disliked (makruh) as they remain divine speech.

Key Terms
غلاف (ghilaf): The wrapper or cover of the mushaf. The ruling on touching depends on whether it is separate or attached.
مس القران (mas al-Quran): Touching the Quran physically. The prohibition applies to the written words, including on objects like dirhams or walls.
حائض (ha'id): A menstruating woman; she is in a state of major impurity and subject to restrictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a menstruating woman touching a mushaf that has a leather cover stitched to its spine?
A) Permissible, because the cover acts as a barrier.
B) Prohibited, because the cover is considered part of the mushaf.
C) Permissible only if she is teaching.
D) Prohibited only if she intends to recite.

Key Takeaway
Touching the Quran without a separate wrapper is haram for the impure; the wrapper must be a distinct covering not attached to the binding.

Taharah — Purification
advanced
10 min
Teaching Quran While Menstruating: Necessity and Intention
Intra-Hanafi dispute on teaching by menstruating woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on a menstruating teacher teaching Quran, distinguishing between the positions of al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi, and state the mufta bihi fatwa.

Core Idea
A menstruating teacher may teach Quran word by word if she does not intend to recite it as worship.

This lesson delves into the specific dispensation for a menstruating female teacher to teach Quran to children. The general prohibition of reciting Quran while in major impurity is lifted due to necessity (darurah). However, scholars differed on the extent: al-Karkhi allowed only word by word, while al-Tahawi allowed half-verse increments. The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) settled on the condition that the teacher must not intend to recite the Quran. Understanding this distinction prevents unnecessary hardship while maintaining respect for the divine word.

Guided Path
1
State the general prohibition and the exception
Normally, a menstruating woman cannot recite Quran (haram). The exception is for teaching, based on necessity (darurah) because menses can be prolonged. Identify the reason for the dispensation.
The source explicitly says 'معللاً بالضرورة مع امتداد الحيض'.
2
Identify the two intra-Hanafi positions
Al-Karkhi: teach word by word with a break between words. Al-Tahawi: teach half a verse, still with separation. Understand what 'half a verse' means: not a full verse, so it avoids being considered recitation.
The source mentions both views from al-Nihayah.
3
Analyze the later scholars' reconciliation
The muta'akhkhirin in al-Khulasah say the most correct (asahh) is that there is no harm if the teacher teaches word by word and his/her intention is not to recite a complete verse. Note the additional condition: intention not to recite Quran.
Some later scholars did not mention the intention condition; it is a refinement.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its scope
The relied-upon fatwa is the permissive view with the condition of not intending Quran recitation. This applies to the menstruating teacher; for the junub, the source indicates more restriction, but al-Khulasah includes him too.
The text says 'واختلف المتأخرون في تعليم الحائض والجنب والأصح أنه لا بأس به...'.
5
Apply to practical teaching scenarios
Consider a teacher saying a phrase like 'بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم' word by word vs. as a full phrase. Also consider teaching a verse like 'إياك نعبد' – can she say it as two words? Know the limits.
The source emphasizes that teaching word by word does not make one a reciter (قارئ).

كتاب الطهارة - باب الحيض
ومسه إلا بغلافه ومنع الحدث المس ومنعهما الجنابة والنفاس وتوطأ بلا غسل بتصرم
قال
والجنب أن يقرأ التوراة والأنجيل. كذا روي عن محمد والطحاوي لا يسلم هذه الرواية . الله رضي عنه وبه يفتى .اهـ. وفي النهاية وغيرها وإذا حاضت المعلمة فينبغي لها أن تعلم الصبيان كلمة كلمة وتقطع بين الكلمتين على قول الكرخي، وعلى قول الطحاوي تعلم نصف آية اهـ. وفي التفريع نظر على قول الكرخي فإنه قائل باستواء الآية وما دونها في المنع إذا كان ذلك بقصد قراءة القرآن وما دون الآية صادق على الكلمة، وإن حمل على التعليم دون قصد القرآن فلا يتقيد بالكلمة ثم في كثير من الكتب التقييد بالحائض المعلمة معللاً بالضرورة مع امتداد الحيض وظاهره عدم الجواز للجنب لكن في الخلاصة: واختلف المتأخرون في تعليم الحائض والجنب والأصح أنه لا بأس به إن كان يلقن كلمة كلمة ولم يكن من قصده يقرأ آية تامة اهـ . والأولى ولم يكن من قصده قراءة القرآن كما لا يخفى . قوله : (ومسه إلا بغلافه) أي تمنع الحائض مس القرآن لما روى الحاكم في المستدرك وقال صحيح الإسناد عن حكيم بن حرام قال : لما بعثني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى اليمن قال : لا تمس القرآن إلا وأنت طاهر واستدلوا له أيضاً بقوله تعالى لا يمسه إلا المطهرون) [الواقعة: ٧٩] فظاهر ما في الكشاف صحة الاستدلال به هنا إن جعلت الجملة صفة للقرآن ولفظه في كتاب مكنون مصون عن غير المقربين من الملائكة لا يطلع عليه من سواهم وهم السراج الوهاج : لا يجوز لهما قراءة التوراة والإنجيل والزبور لأن الكل كلام الله تعالى. قوله : (قال رضي الله عنه الخ) أي صاحب الخلاصة قوله : ( وفي التفريغ نظر (الخ قال في النهر أقول : بل هو صحيح إذ الكرخي وإن منع ما دون الآية لكن بما به يسمى قارئاً ولذا قالوا لا يكره التهجي بالقراءة، ولا يخفى أنه بالتعليم كلمة لا يعد قارئاً فتنبه لهذا التقييد المفيد .اهـ. ونقل بعض الفضلاء عن المولى يعقوب باشا ما نصه : قوله ما دون الآية أي من المركبات لا المفردات لأنه جوّز للحائض المعلمة تعليمه كلمة كلمة .اهـ. وهذا مؤيد لما قاله صاحب النهر، وكذا يؤيده ما في شرح المنية حيث حمل قولها ولا يكره التهجي للجنب بالقرآن والتعلم للصبيان حرفاً حرفاً أي كلمة كلمة . القطع بين كل كلمتين على قول الكرخي، وعلى قول الطحاوي لا يكره إذا علم نصف آية مع القطع بينهما. وقال قبله : وينبغي أن تقيد الآية بالقصيرة التي ليس ما دونها مقدار ثلاث آيات قصار فإنه إذا قرأ مقدار سورة الكوثر يعد قارئاً وإن كان دون آية حتى جازت به الصلاة اهـ. وفي السراج قال أصحابنا المتأخرون : إذا كانت الحائض أو النفساء معلمة جاز لها أن تلقن الصبيان كلمة كلمة وتقطع بين الكلمتين على قول الكرخي، وعلى قول الطحاوي تعلمهم نصف آية نص آية ولا تلقنهم آية تامة قوله : ( والأولى ولم يكن من قصده قراءة القرآن قال بعض الفضلاء: في اشتراط صاحب عدم قصد القراءة نظر، لأنه إذا لم يقصد القراءة فلا يتقيد بالكلمة لما تقدم أن القرآن يخرج عن القرآنية بالقصد ولم يذكر هذا الشرط في النهاية والسراج والظهيرية والذخيرة، وكذا في فتح
المطهرون من جميع الأدناس أدناس الذنوب، وما سواها إن جعلت الجملة صفة لكتاب مكنون وهو اللوح، وإن جعلتها صفة للقرآن فالمعنى لا ينبغي أن يمسه إلا من هو على الطهارة من الناس يعني مس المكتوب منه ا هـ . لكن الإمام الطيبي في حاشيته ذكر صحة الاستدلال به على الوجه الأوّل أيضاً فقال : فالمعنى على الوجه الأوّل أن هذا الكتاب كريم على الله تعالى ومن كرمه أنه أثبته عنده في اللوح المحفوظ وعظم شأنه بأن حكم بأنه لا يمسه إلا الملائكة المقربون وصانه عن غير المقربين فيجب أن يكون حكمه عند الناس كذلك بناء على أن ترتب الحكم على الوصف المناسب مشعر بالعلية لأن سياق الكلام لتعظيم شأن القرآن. وعن الدارمي عن عبد الله أن بن عمرو النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال القرآن أحب إلى الله تعالى من السموات والأرض ومن فيهن ا هـ . وذكر أنه على الوجه الثاني إخبار في معنى الأمر كقوله الزاني لا ينكح إلا زانية) [النور: ٣] ١ هـ. وتعبير المصنف بمس القرآن أولى من تعبير غيره بمس المصحف لشمول كلامه ما إذا مس لوحاً مكتوباً عليه آية وكذا الدرهم والحائط، وتقييده بالسورة في الهداية اتفاقي بل المراد الآية لكن لا يجوز مس المصحف كله المكتوب وغيره بخلاف غيره فإنه لا يمنع إلا مس المكتوب. كذا ذكره في السراج الوهاج مع أن في الأول اختلافاً فقال في غاية البيان وقال بعض مشايخنا المعتبر حقيقة المكتوب حتى إن مس ومس مواضع البياض لا يكره لأنه لم يمس القرآن وهذا أقرب إلى القياس والمنع أقرب إلى التعظيم ا هـ . وفي تفسير الغلاف اختلاف؛ فقيل الجلد المشرز، وفي غاية البيان مصحف مشرز أجزاؤه مشدود بعضها إلى بعض من الشيرازة وليست بعربية، وفي الكافي والغلاف الجلد الذي عليه في الأصح، وقيل هو المنفصل كالخريطة ونحوها المتصل بالمصحف منه حتى يدخل في بيعه بلا ذكر ا هـ . وصحح هذا القول في الهداية وكثير من الكتب وزاد في القدير ولم أر من نبه على ذلك فليتأمل قوله : (قول المصنف ومسه إلا بغلافه) قال في النهر : ولم أر في كلامهم حكم مس باقي الكتب كالتوراة ونحوها فظاهر استدلالهم بالآية اختصاص المنع بالقرآن اهـ. وفي حاشية الرملي: وهل يجوز في المنسوخ أن يمسه المحدث أو يتلوه الجنب فيه تردد والأشبه جوازه فيما نسخ تلاوته وأقر حكمه لأنه ليس بقرآن إجماعاً كما في شرح مختصر الأصول لابن الحاجب للعضد، وإذا كان هذا فيما أقر حكمه فمن باب أولى الجواز فيما نسخ تلاوته وحكمه اهـ أقول: ولا يخفى عليك بما قدمناه من العلامة الحلبي وغيره أن المنع من تلاوة المنسوخ من القرآن أولى، ثم رأيت بعض الفضلاء قال المشهور أن العلامة العضد شافعي فلا يصلح ما قاله دليلاً لمذهبنا، وقد تقدم أن ما نسخ تلاوته وحكمه كالتوارة ونحوها فتلاوته للجنب ومن بمعناه مكروهة على الصحيح كما اعتمده الحلبي لأن ما بدل منه بعض غير معين وكونه منسوخاً لا يخرجه عن كونه كلام الله تعالى كالآيات المنسوخة من القرآن، وأما مسه فقد علم حكمه مما نقله القهستاني عن الذخيرة
And touching it except with its wrapper, and the event prevents touching, and both (menstruation and post-partum) and janabah prevent touching, and she (menstruating woman) is entered without bath (but) with (time) passing. He said: And the junub should not read the Torah and the Gospel. Thus it is narrated from Muhammad and al-Tahawi, but this narration is not sound; (al-Allamah?) may Allah be pleased with him, and with it fatwa is given. End. In al-Nihayah and others: And when a female teacher menstruates, it is appropriate for her to teach the boys word by word and separate between two words according to al-Karkhi, and according to al-Tahawi she teaches half a verse. End. And in al-Tafri', there is consideration (that) according to al-Karkhi, for he holds that the verse and what is less than it are equal in prohibition if that is with the intention of reciting the Quran, and what is less than a verse applies to a word; and if it is carried on teaching without intention of Quran, it is not restricted to a word. Then in many books there is restriction to the menstruating female teacher, justified by necessity with prolongation of menses, and its apparent meaning is that it is not permissible for the junub. But in al-Khulasah: And the later scholars differed about teaching of the menstruating woman and the junub, and the most correct is that there is no harm if he teaches word by word and his intention was not to recite a complete verse. End. And the better (view) is that his intention was not to recite the Quran, as is not hidden. His statement: (And touching it except with its wrapper) meaning the menstruating woman is prevented from touching the Quran because of what al-Hakim narrated in al-Mustadrak and said it is authentic chain from Hakim ibn Hizam who said: When the Messenger of Allah sent me to Yemen, he said: Do not touch the Quran unless you are pure. And they also used as proof His statement: 'None touch it except the purified' [al-Waqi'ah:79]. So the apparent meaning of what is in al-Kashshaf is the validity of using it as proof here if the sentence is made a description of the Quran and its wording in a hidden Book preserved from other than the near ones of the angels, none can see it except them. And al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: It is not permissible for them (menstruating woman and junub) to read the Torah, Gospel, and Psalms because all are the speech of Allah. His statement: (He said, may Allah be pleased with him, etc.) meaning the author of al-Khulasah. His statement: (And in al-Tafri', there is consideration) etc. He said in al-Nahr: I say: Rather it is correct, for al-Karkhi, even if he prohibits what is less than a verse, but it is by that which he is called a reciter, so they said it is not disliked to spell (letters) in recitation, and it is not hidden that by teaching word by word he is not considered a reciter, so be mindful of this beneficial restriction. End. And some virtuous people narrated from al-Mawla Ya'qub Pasha what follows: His statement: 'what is less than a verse' meaning from compounds, not singulars, because he permitted for the menstruating female teacher to teach it word by word. End. And this supports what the author of al-Nahr said, and likewise what is in Sharh al-Munyah supports it where it carries her saying: And it is not disliked to spell (letters) for the junub with the Quran and teaching boys letter by letter, i.e., word by word, with separation between every two words according to al-Karkhi, and according to al-Tahawi it is not disliked if he teaches half a verse with separation between them. And he said before it: It is appropriate to restrict the verse to the short one that does not have what is less than it equal to three short verses, for if he recites the amount of Surat al-Kawthar, he is considered a reciter even if it is less than a verse, until prayer is permissible with it. End. In al-Siraj: Our later scholars said: If the menstruating or post-partum woman is a teacher, it is permissible for her to dictate to the boys word by word and separate between two words according to al-Karkhi, and according to al-Tahawi they teach them half a verse, a complete verse, and do not teach them a complete verse. His statement: (And the better (view) is that his intention is not to recite the Quran). Some virtuous people said: There is consideration in the condition of the author of not intending recitation, because if he does not intend recitation, then it is not restricted to a word, as previously mentioned that the Quran exits from being Quran by intention, and this condition is not mentioned in al-Nihayah, al-Siraj, al-Zahiriyyah, al-Dhakhirah, nor in Fath. The purified from all impurities, the impurities of sins, and other than that if the sentence is made a description of a hidden Book, which is the Preserved Tablet, and if it is made a description of the Quran, then the meaning is: it is not befitting that it should be touched except by one who is in a state of purity from people, meaning touching the written part. End. But Imam al-Tayyibi in his gloss mentioned the validity of using it as proof on the first aspect as well, saying: The meaning on the first aspect is that this Book is noble in the sight of Allah, and from its nobility is that He established it with Him in the Preserved Tablet and magnified its rank by ruling that none touch it except the near angels, and He protected it from other than the near ones, so it is necessary that its ruling among people be likewise, based on that arranging the ruling upon the appropriate description indicates causation, because the context of the speech is to magnify the rank of the Quran. And from al-Darimi from 'Abdullah ibn 'Amr (?) that the Prophet said: The Quran is more beloved to Allah than the heavens and the earth and those in them. End. And he mentioned that on the second aspect it is a report in the sense of a command, like His statement: 'The adulterer does not marry except an adulteress' [al-Nur:3]. End. And the expression of the author with 'touching the Quran' is better than others' expression with 'touching the mushaf' because his speech includes if one touches a tablet on which a verse is written, and likewise a dirham and a wall, and his restriction to the surah in al-Hidayah is incidental, rather the intended meaning is the verse. But it is not permissible to touch all the mashif written and others, unlike other things, for it does not prevent except touching the written. Thus it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, although there is a difference in the first: In Ghayat al-Bayan: And some of our shaykhs said: What is considered is the reality of the written, such that if one touches the white spaces, it is not disliked because he did not touch the Quran, and this is closer to analogy, and prohibition is closer to veneration. End. And in the interpretation of the wrapper there is difference: It is said it is the stitched leather, and in Ghayat al-Bayan: A mushaf with stitched parts, some parts bound to others from al-shirazah, and it is not Arabic. In al-Kafi: The wrapper in the most correct view is the leather that is on it, and it is said it is the separate one like a pouch and similar that is attached to the mushaf so that it is included in its sale without mention. End. And this view is certified in al-Hidayah and many books, and increased in al-Qadir: And I have not seen anyone who pointed that out, so let it be considered. His statement: (The author's statement: 'And touching it except with its wrapper') He said in al-Nahr: I have not seen in their speech the ruling on touching the remaining books like the Torah and the like. The apparent meaning of their using the verse as proof is the restriction of the prohibition to the Quran. End. In al-Ramli's gloss: And is it permissible for the one in hadath to touch the abrogated or for the junub to recite it? There is hesitation, and the more similar is its permissibility in what has been abrogated in recitation and its ruling remains, because it is not Quran by consensus, as in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Usul of Ibn al-Hajib by al-'Adud. And if this is in what its ruling remains, then a fortiori permissibility in what has been abrogated in recitation and ruling. End. I say: It is not hidden from you, from what we have presented from al-Allamah al-Halabi and others, that prohibition of reciting the abrogated part of the Quran is more appropriate. Then I saw some virtuous people said: The widespread view is that al-'Allamah al-'Adud is Shafi'i, so what he said cannot be a proof for our school. And it has preceded that what has been abrogated in recitation and ruling like the Torah and the like, its recitation by the junub and those like him is disliked on the correct view, as al-Halabi relied on, because some part of it has been replaced by something non-specific, and being abrogated does not remove it from being the speech of Allah, like the abrogated verses of the Quran. As for touching it, its ruling is known from what al-Qahistani narrated from al-Dhakhirah.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a Hanafi commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addresses the restrictions on a menstruating woman (ha'id) and a person in a state of major impurity (junub) regarding sacred texts. The discussion is organized around several rulings from the matn. Firstly, touching the Quran is prohibited without a wrapper (ghilaf). The proof is a hadith from Hakim ibn Hizam and the Quranic verse (56:79) 'None touch it except the purified.' The commentary explores different interpretations of the verse, whether it refers to the Preserved Tablet or the mushaf, and concludes that it supports the prohibition for the impure. Secondly, the matn indicates that a junub should not read the Torah, Gospel, or Psalms, as they are all divine speech. However, there is a minority narration from Muhammad and al-Tahawi that is not relied upon; the fatwa is on the prohibition. Thirdly, a significant portion discusses the permissibility of a menstruating female teacher teaching Quran to children. The text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Karkhi allows teaching word by word with a break between words, while al-Tahawi allows teaching half a verse. The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) lean towards permissibility with conditions, especially if the teacher does not intend to recite Quran but merely teach. The commentary emphasizes that the dispensation is due to necessity (darurah) as her menses may be prolonged. For a junub, there is more restriction. Fourthly, the definition of 'wrapper' (ghilaf) is discussed: whether it is the leather cover attached to the mushaf or a separate pouch. The most correct view is the separate covering, and it affects the ruling on touching. Finally, the passage touches on touching and reciting abrogated (mansukh) scriptures: there is hesitation, but the relied-upon view is that it is permissible to touch what has been abrogated in recitation but whose ruling remains, because it is no longer Quran. However, for the junub, reciting even abrogated parts is disliked (makruh) as they remain divine speech.

Key Terms
الحائض المعلمة (al-ha'id al-mu'allimah): A female teacher who is menstruating; the subject of the dispensation.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that permits the normally prohibited, here due to prolonged menses.
القصد (al-qasd): Intention; the later scholars condition that the teacher must not intend to recite Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi fatwa (muta'akhkhirin), which condition is essential for a menstruating teacher to teach Quran?
A) She must be in a state of wudu.
B) She must teach word by word and not intend to recite Quran.
C) She must only teach from memory, not from a mushaf.
D) She must not teach more than half a verse.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating teacher may teach Quran word by word due to necessity, provided she does not intend to recite it as an act of worship.

Quranic Evidence for Prohibition of Touching the Quran Without Wudu
Explaining the Quranic evidence and its application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi proof from the Quran for the prohibition of touching the Quran without wudu and explain the scope of the prohibition, including its application to coins, boards, and walls with written verses.

Core Idea
Touching the Quran without wudu is haram, as the verse 'لا يمسه إلا المطهرون' is interpreted as a command for purity.

In this lesson, we explore the primary evidence for the Hanafi ruling that it is haram to touch the Quran without wudu. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq examines the Quranic verse 'لا يمسه إلا المطهرون' and presents two interpretations that together establish the prohibition. We also learn that the ruling extends beyond the mushaf to any surface bearing Quranic verses, such as boards, coins, or walls. Understanding this proof strengthens your ability to apply the ruling correctly and appreciate the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verse and its two interpretations
Locate the verse 'لا يمسه إلا المطهرون' in the passage. Note that it can refer to the Preserved Tablet (al-Lawh al-Mahfuz) or to the Quran itself. Understand that both interpretations are used to derive the ruling for humans.
The first interpretation relates to angels; the second directly addresses humans.
2
Analyze how each interpretation supports the prohibition
For the first interpretation, learn how Imam al-Tibi uses the principle that attaching a ruling to a suitable description indicates causation. Since the Quran is honored by being touched only by pure angels, humans must also be pure. For the second interpretation, recognize that the verse is an informative statement carrying a command, similar to 'The adulterer shall not marry except an adulteress'.
This shows the Quranic basis for the requirement of wudu.
3
Understand the broader scope: 'mas al-Quran' vs 'mas al-mushaf'
The author prefers the expression 'touching the Quran' because it includes any object with a written verse—boards, coins, walls—not just the mushaf. This is a practical expansion of the ruling.
The prohibition applies only to the written text, not blank areas.
4
Apply the ruling to specific cases
Consider hypothetical scenarios: touching a coin with a verse, a board in a classroom, or a wall in a mosque. In each case, the Hanafi ruling is that it is haram without wudu, because they are instances of 'mas al-Quran'.
This step reinforces the practical application.
5
Evaluate the authority and status of this ruling
Note that this is the position from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school. Some early scholars considered it makruh, but the Hanafi view is relied upon.
Understanding the hierarchy of authority is essential for usul al-ifta.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة - باب الحيض ٣٤٩ المطهرون من جميع الأدناس أدناس الذنوب، وما سواها إن جعلت الجملة صفة لكتاب مكنون وهو اللوح، وإن جعلتها صفة للقرآن فالمعنى لا ينبغي أن يمسه إلا من هو على الطهارة من الناس يعني مس المكتوب منه ا هـ . لكن الإمام الطيبي في حاشيته ذكر صحة الاستدلال به على الوجه الأوّل أيضاً فقال : فالمعنى على الوجه الأوّل أن هذا الكتاب كريم على الله تعالى ومن كرمه أنه أثبته عنده في اللوح المحفوظ وعظم شأنه بأن حكم بأنه لا يمسه إلا الملائكة المقربون وصانه عن غير المقربين فيجب أن يكون حكمه عند الناس كذلك بناء على أن ترتب الحكم على الوصف المناسب مشعر بالعلية لأن سياق الكلام لتعظيم شأن القرآن. وعن الدارمي عن عبد الله أن بن عمرو النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال القرآن أحب إلى الله تعالى من السموات والأرض ومن فيهن ا هـ . وذكر أنه على الوجه الثاني إخبار في معنى الأمر كقوله الزاني لا ينكح إلا زانية) [النور: ٣] ١ هـ. وتعبير المصنف بمس القرآن أولى من تعبير غيره بمس المصحف لشمول كلامه ما إذا مس لوحاً مكتوباً عليه آية وكذا الدرهم والحائط، وتقييده بالسورة في الهداية اتفاقي بل المراد الآية لكن لا يجوز مس المصحف كله المكتوب وغيره بخلاف غيره فإنه لا يمنع إلا مس المكتوب. كذا ذكره في السراج الوهاج
The Book of Purification - Chapter of Menstruation [349]. The purified ones from all impurities, impurities of sins and others. If the sentence is made a description of the hidden Book (al-Lawh al-Mahfuz), then the meaning is that only those who are in a state of purity from among the people should touch it, meaning the written part. End. But Imam al-Tibi in his commentary mentioned the validity of using it as evidence according to the first interpretation as well, saying: The meaning according to the first interpretation is that this book is honored by Allah, and from its honor is that He established it with Him in the Preserved Tablet and magnified its status by decreeing that none may touch it except the angels brought near, and protected it from others. So its ruling with people must be likewise, based on the fact that attaching a ruling to an appropriate description indicates causation, because the context is exalting the Quran. And from al-Darimi through Abdullah that Ibn Amr (?) from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: The Quran is more beloved to Allah than the heavens and the earth and what is in them. End. And he mentioned that according to the second interpretation, it is an informative statement in the meaning of a command, like His saying: 'The adulterer shall not marry except an adulteress' [al-Nur: 3]. End. The author's expression 'touching the Quran' is better than others' expression 'touching the mushaf', because it includes the case of touching a board on which a verse is written, likewise a coin and a wall. And his restriction to a surah in al-Hidayah is accidental; rather the intended meaning is a verse. But it is not permissible to touch the entire mushaf, written and other, unlike other things, which only prevent touching the written part. Thus it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the evidence for the prohibition of touching the Quran without wudu. It begins by discussing the Quranic verse 'لا يمسه إلا المطهرون' (None touch it except the purified). The author presents two interpretations: first, that it refers to the Preserved Tablet and the angels; second, that it refers to the Quran itself and commands humans to be pure when touching it. Imam al-Tibi supports the first interpretation by analogy: if the Quran is so honored that only angels touch it in the heavens, then humans must also honor it by touching it only in a state of purity. This is based on the principle that attaching a ruling to an appropriate description indicates causation (العقلاء يستدلون بذلك). The second interpretation is that the verse is in the form of an informative statement but carries a command, similar to the verse about adulterers. The author then notes that the expression 'touching the Quran' is broader than 'touching the mushaf,' as it includes any writing containing Quranic verses, even on a board, coin, or wall. However, the prohibition only applies to the written text itself, not the margins or blank spaces, as stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.

Key Terms
مس القرآن (mas al-Quran): Touching the Quran, including any writing containing Quranic verses, even on a board or coin.
المطهرون (al-mutahharun): The purified ones, here interpreted as angels in the first interpretation and as humans with wudu in the second.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for touching a coin on which a Quranic verse is written without wudu?
A) Permissible because it is a coin
B) Impermissible because it is considered touching the Quran
C) Permissible only if the coin is in a cover
D) Makruh but not haram

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school derives the prohibition of touching the Quran without wudu from the verse 'لا يمسه إلا المطهرون', interpreting it as a command for purity, and extends this to any writing containing Quranic verses.

Touching the Mushaf and Sharia Books: Cover, Sleeve, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on touching the Quran and sharia books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on touching the Quran through a cover or sleeve and distinguish the permissibility for other sharia books, including the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Touching the mushaf through a sleeve is prohibitedly disliked; for sharia books it is permitted with a sleeve but not without, except tafsir.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the detailed rulings on touching the Quran and other religious texts. It addresses the definition of the cover (ghilaf), the use of a sleeve or handkerchief, and an intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding books of hadith and fiqh. Understanding this discussion is essential for a nuanced application of taharah rules in daily scholarly practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objects and Legal Categories
Discern the different objects discussed: the mushaf itself (including blank spaces and cover), the sleeve or handkerchief as barriers, and other sharia books (tafsir, hadith, fiqh, grammar). Each has a distinct ruling.
2
Define Key Terms: Ghilaf (Cover) and Its Ruling
Understand the difference between an attached cover (musharraz) that is considered part of the mushaf and a separate cover (like a case). The attached cover has the same ruling as the mushaf, while a separate cover does not.
Al-Hidayah adopts the view that the attached cover is part of the mushaf.
3
Analyze the Ruling on Touching the Mushaf with a Sleeve or Handkerchief
Apply the principle that if the barrier moves with the body (e.g., a sleeve or handkerchief held by its edge), it is legally treated as part of the body, making touching the mushaf prohibitedly disliked. If it does not move with the body, it is a valid barrier.
This is analogous to the turban with impurity case.
4
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sharia Books
Compare the positions: Abu Hanifa holds that touching books of hadith and fiqh without wudu is not disliked, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it disliked. The reason given is that these books contain Quranic verses. The relied-upon view permits touching with a sleeve due to necessity, but recommends wudu for veneration.
Tafsir books are an exception even with a sleeve; they require wudu.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and Recommended Practice
The operative ruling is that touching sharia books with a sleeve is permissible, but the recommended practice is to avoid even that and perform wudu. This is based on the principle of ta'zim (veneration) as exemplified by early scholars like al-Halwani and al-Sarakhsi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مع أن في الأول اختلافاً فقال في غاية البيان وقال بعض مشايخنا المعتبر حقيقة المكتوب حتى إن مس ومس مواضع البياض لا يكره لأنه لم يمس القرآن وهذا أقرب إلى القياس والمنع أقرب إلى التعظيم ا هـ . وفي تفسير الغلاف اختلاف؛ فقيل الجلد المشرز، وفي غاية البيان مصحف مشرز أجزاؤه مشدود بعضها إلى بعض من الشيرازة وليست بعربية، وفي الكافي والغلاف الجلد الذي عليه في الأصح، وقيل هو المنفصل كالخريطة ونحوها المتصل بالمصحف منه حتى يدخل في بيعه بلا ذكر ا هـ . وصحح هذا القول في الهداية وكثير من الكتب وزاد في فتح القدير: والمراد بالكراهة كراهة التحريم ولهذا عبر بنفي الجواز في الفتاوى. وقال لي بعض الاخوان : هل يجوز مس المصحف بمنديل هو لابسه على عنقه؟ قلت : لا أعلم فيه منقولاً والذي يظهر أنه إن كان بطرفه وهو يتحرك بحركته ينبغي أن لا يجوز، وإن كان لا يتحرك بحركته ينبغي أن يجوز لاعتبارهم إياه في الأوّل تابعاً له كبدنه دون الثاني . قالوا فيمن صلى وعليه عمامة بطرفها نجاسة مانعة إن كان ألقاه وهو يتحرك لا يجوز وإلا يجوز اعتباراً له على ما ذكرنا ا وفي الهداية بخلاف كتب الشريعة حيث يرخص لأهلها في مسها بالكم لأن فيه ضرورة ا هـ . وفي فتح القدير: إنه يقتضي أنه لا يرخص بلا كم قالوا يكره مس كتب التفسير والفقه والسنن لأنها لا تخلو عن آيات القرآن وهذا التعليل يمنع مس شروح النحو أيضاً ا هـ . وفي الخلاصة : يكره مس كتب الأحاديث والفقه للمحدث عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة الأصح أنه لا يكره، ذكره من كتاب الصلاة في فضل القراءة خارج الصلاة وفي شرح الدرر والغزر : ورخص المس باليد في الكتب الشرعية إلا التفسير ذكره في مجمع الفتاوى وغيرها السراج الوهاج معزياً إلى الحواشي المستحب أن لا يأخذ كتب الشريعة بالكم أيضاً بل يجدد الوضوء كلما أحدث وهذا أقرب إلى التعظيم . قال :الحلواني : إنما نلت هذا العلم بالتعظيم فإني ما أخذت الكاغد إلا بطهارة والإمام السرخسي كان مبطوناً في ليلة وكان يكرر درس كتابه فتوضأ في تلك الليلة سبعة عشرة مرة . هـ . وفي فروع من التعظيم أن لا يمد رجله إلى الكتاب.
Although there is a difference regarding the first: in Ghayat al-Bayan it is said, 'Some of our scholars considered that what matters is the reality of the written, such that touching the blank spaces is not disliked because he did not touch the Quran. This is closer to analogy, while prohibition is closer to veneration.' End. And regarding the interpretation of al-ghilaf (cover), there is a difference; it is said it is the stitched leather cover (musharraz). In Ghayat al-Bayan: 'A mushaf with its parts stitched and bound together from the binding (shirazah), which is not Arabic.' In al-Kafi and al-Ghilaf: 'The cover is the leather that is on it, according to the more correct view.' And it is said it is separate, like a case and the like, attached to the mushaf from it, so that it enters into its sale without mention. End. This view was adopted in al-Hidayah and many books, and in Fath al-Qadir it is added: 'And what is meant by karahah (dislike) is karahah of prohibition (tahrim), and therefore he expressed it by negating permissibility in the fatawa.' A brother asked me: 'Is it permissible to touch the mushaf with a handkerchief worn around the neck?' I said: 'I do not know of any transmitted ruling. What appears is that if it is held by its edge and moves with his movement, it should not be permissible. If it does not move with his movement, it should be permissible, because they consider it in the first case as a follower like his body, unlike the second.' They said regarding one who prays with a turban on which there is an impurity that prevents: if it is worn and moves, it is not permissible; otherwise it is permissible, based on our reasoning. End. In al-Hidayah: 'Unlike the books of sharia, where it is permitted for their people to touch them with a sleeve because there is a necessity.' End. And in Fath al-Qadir: 'This implies that it is not permitted without a sleeve. They said it is disliked to touch books of tafsir, fiqh, and sunan because they are not free from Quranic verses, and this reasoning would also prevent touching grammatical commentaries.' End. In al-Khulasah: 'Touching books of hadith and fiqh for a person without wudu is disliked according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Hanifa, the soundest view is that it is not disliked.' Mentioned from the Book of Prayer in the chapter on the virtue of reading outside prayer. In Sharh al-Durar wa al-Ghurar: 'Permission to touch with the hand (without wudu) is given for sharia books except tafsir.' Mentioned in Majma' al-Fatawa and elsewhere, citing al-Siraj al-Wahhaj from the marginal notes: 'It is recommended not to take sharia books with the sleeve either, but to renew wudu every time one has an impurity, and this is closer to veneration.' Al-Halwani said: 'I only attained this knowledge through veneration; I never took paper except in a state of purity.' And Imam al-Sarakhsi had diarrhea one night and repeated his lesson; he performed wudu seventeen times that night. End. And among the branches of veneration is that he should not stretch his leg towards the book.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding touching the Quran and other religious books. It first discusses the difference about touching blank spaces on the Quran: some scholars consider only the written text prohibited, not the margins, which is closer to qiyas; but prohibition is closer to ta'zim (veneration). Then it addresses the definition of ghilaf (cover): whether it is the permanent binding (musharraz) or a separate case. The adopted view in al-Hidayah is that the cover has the same ruling as the mushaf. The text clarifies that the 'dislike' for touching with a sleeve is actually karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitory dislike), meaning it is haram. A practical case is discussed: touching the mushaf with a handkerchief worn around the neck. The ruling depends on whether the handkerchief moves with the person's movement. If it does, it is considered a part of the body and thus prohibits touching; if not, it is permissible. This is analogous to the case of a turban with impurity. The passage then addresses books of sharia (hadith, fiqh, tafsir). According to al-Hidayah, it is permitted to touch them with a sleeve due to necessity, which implies it is not permitted without a sleeve. There is a difference between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): the disciples consider it disliked (makruh) to touch such books without wudu, while Abu Hanifa holds it is not disliked. However, the recommended practice is veneration: to avoid even taking books with a sleeve and to renew wudu. The account of al-Halwani and al-Sarakhsi exemplifies this high level of respect. Finally, a point of etiquette: not to stretch one's leg towards a book.

Key Terms
الغلاف (al-ghilaf): The cover of the mushaf, which may be attached (musharraz) or separate. The attached cover has the same ruling as the mushaf.
الكم (al-kumm): The sleeve of a garment. Touching the mushaf with a sleeve is considered, but the sleeve is a follower of the body.
كراهة التحريم (karahah al-tahrim): Prohibitory dislike, meaning the act is practically haram but not as severe as clear haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on touching a book of tafsir without wudu using only the hand?
A) Permissible because tafsir is not Quran
B) Permissible only with a sleeve
C) Disliked (makruh) because it contains Quranic verses
D) Haram under all circumstances

Key Takeaway
Touching the mushaf with a sleeve is prohibitory disliked; for other sharia books it is permitted with a sleeve, but the recommended practice is to maintain wudu out of veneration.
